  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7ef25648-0b1e-4996-8fcb-ff4a1856a1fc'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer14008242940954433364">It's the end of the world. Six students have taken cover in Cortege High but shelter is little comfort when the dead outside won't stop pounding on the doors. One bite is all it takes to kill a person and bring them back as a monstrous version of their former self. To Sloane Price, that doesn't sound so bad. Six months ago, <i>her </i>world collapsed and since then, she's failed </span>
  <span id="freeText14008242940954433364" style="display:none">It's the end of the world. Six students have taken cover in Cortege High but shelter is little comfort when the dead outside won't stop pounding on the doors. One bite is all it takes to kill a person and bring them back as a monstrous version of their former self. To Sloane Price, that doesn't sound so bad. Six months ago, <i>her </i>world collapsed and since then, she's failed to find a reason to keep going. Now seems like the perfect time to give up. As Sloane eagerly waits for the barricades to fall, she's forced to witness the apocalypse through the eyes of five people who actually <i>want </i>to live. But as the days crawl by, the motivations for survival change in startling ways and soon the group's fate is determined less and less by what's happening outside and more and more by the unpredictable and violent bids for life—<i>and </i>death—inside. When everything is gone, what do <i>you </i>hold on to?</span>
  <a data-text-id="14008242940954433364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/71265772-summer-summers"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/71265772-summer-summers">Summer Summers</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The real answer is that there are some slightly inappropriate scenes. However, should you wish to not read those, they last mostly a page and a half w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The real answer is that there are some slightly inappropriate scenes. However, should you wish to not read those, they last mostly a page and a half when they happen. There are no sexual relations that do take place though only heated makeout sessions. It is a YA after all and even though they are there they end quickly. <br /><br />They can easily be skipped as they really do not do anything but spice up the reading. As far as cussing, yes there is some cussing. I think that is reasonable considering they are in the middle of a zombie apocalypse which is always a stressful way of living.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=zombies-r-bitey">zombies-r-bitey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=thank-you-bea-or-ala">thank-you-bea-or-ala</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=upstairs-neighbors">upstairs-neighbors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361616069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6601941232369573313">this isn't a zombie book so much as a zombie framing device to explore damage and the difficulties of making yourself vulnerable in front of someone - of communication's pitfalls and the numbing effects of trauma. <br/><br/>there are people who believe that trauma builds character. these people have probably never experienced trauma. trauma does not build character, but how someone responds to trauma is the true and most telling test of character.<br/><br/>more often than not, trauma leads to a retreat. nobody is a</span>
  <span id="freeText6601941232369573313" style="display:none">this isn't a zombie book so much as a zombie framing device to explore damage and the difficulties of making yourself vulnerable in front of someone - of communication's pitfalls and the numbing effects of trauma. <br><br>there are people who believe that trauma builds character. these people have probably never experienced trauma. trauma does not build character, but how someone responds to trauma is the true and most telling test of character.<br><br>more often than not, trauma leads to a retreat. nobody is a fan of emotional outpourings, are they? or am i projecting again? so let's just talk about this character. <i>sloane</i> is not a fan of emotional outpourings. her father has been physically abusing sloane and her sister for years, and the two of them formed this intensely close bond that never allowed anyone else in. after her sister ran away, leaving sloane alone in the path of her father's rage, she had no support system in place to fill the gap, and became suicidal.<br><br>and then, the zombies attacked.<br><br>so what happens when the wrong people survive?? the ones who didn't want to survive <i>before</i> the world went to hell?<br><br>this is a fascinating character study. six teenagers holed up in a school, barricading the doors against the zombie invasion outside. alliances will form, resentments will fester, desperate hookups and confessions and all-around brokenness will ensue.<br><br>and sloane, watching it all, unable to break through her own emotional reserves to make herself vulnerable in front of the others. <br><br><i>is this what it's like to get close to other people - you do something insane together and then you have to share everything even if you don't really want to?</i><br><br>she grows so much as a character, and it is painful and sad and you just want to <i>be</i> there with her, holding her throughout it all. not that she'd let you. <br><br>the other characters are great, too. this is not a one-person show. it manages to rejuvenate the YA-survival genre for me, like a cross between <i>the breakfast club</i> and a way more intense <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8428140.Trapped" title="Trapped by Michael Northrop" rel="nofollow noopener">Trapped</a>.<br><br>one character mourns his life, and how with nothing left in the world, his opportunities to <i>become</i> something have pretty much ended.<br><br><i>"...it's nothing. i thought it could be something, i mean, eventually." he finally looks at us. "my life. i thought - but i mean...it's nothing."</i><br><br>how absolutely shattering to realize, at fifteen, that your life has meant nothing and is essentially over. GAH!<br><br>and how clear-eyed sloane is through it all, as she thinks of a future she is still not sure she wants any part of.<br><br><i>when this is over, society will need entertainment to get past it. we'll make movies about it, hundreds of movies, and in every one of them, we'll be the heroes and the love interests and best friends and winners and we'll watch these movies until we are so far removed from our own history, we'll forget how it really felt to be here.</i><br><br>that insight is very rare in these typical survival novels. often, it is just all about the clinging to a member of the opposite sex for validation or comfort. and there is some of that, here, but it is way more charged than is typical. there is an immediacy and a desperation that is deeply written and felt by the reader. <br><br>and thank you for the realism:<br><br><i>the thing no one tells you about surviving, about the mere act of holding out, is how many hours are nothing because nothing happens.they also don't tell you about how you can share your deepest secrets with someone, kiss them, and the next hour it's like there's nothing between you because not everything can mean something all the time or you'd be crushed under the weight of it. they don't tell you how you will float through days. you autopilot, here but not really here, sleepwalking, and then every so often you are awake.</i><br><br>god, i am so tired of <i>import</i>. there is an awful lot of sleeping in this book. and silence. and yet it is not boring to read - this is such a fast-paced book. but the reality of how boring it would be to survive is much appreciated, and the true fact that not every kiss is the beginning and end of everything. a kiss can be, in fact, just a kiss...<br><br>and this. the ramifications of the last two sentences in this quote are quite easy to overlook if you haven't read the book, but:<br><br><i>i am caked in mud and my hair is straggly and knotted from the rain. my lips are bruised. there are cuts and scratches on me that i must have gotten since leaving the school but i don't remember how. she won't recognize me when she sees me. i look like someone who has survived.</i><br><br>you should read the book.<br><br>if nothing else, read the first chapter, which is a triumph of buildup and utter utter chaos. i cannot remember ever reading a better opening chapter in all my days.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6601941232369573313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12318197085479837652"><br/><b>HARROWING.</b> I sincerely never thought that I could ever be so fascinated by a zombie post-apocalyptic story before, but there’s a first to everything, isn’t there? However, it’s definitely more focused on the psychological elements than the world-building, since it underlines the theme of survival and how precious and fragile life is. Courtney Summers, you’re writing terribly tearful stories. Please don’t stop. </span>

<div id="review_199889319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199889319" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199889319?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199889319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5370463818902947329"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>4.5</b><br/><br/>I owe a huge thanks to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers' title='Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Summers</a> for giving me a second chance to read and review this after my netgalley rejection. It made my day and I'm so glad <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_Is_Not_a_Test' title='This Is Not a Test by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Is Not a Test</a> was all that I'd hoped it would be.<br/><br/>I'm going to say what I said at the start of my reviews or before I started reading: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7094569.Feed__Newsflesh_Trilogy__1_' title='Feed (Newsflesh Trilogy #1) by Mira Grant' rel='nofollow noopener'>Feed</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_' title='The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9554790.The_Other_Life__The_Other_Life___1_' title='The Other Life (The Other Life, #1) by Susanne Winnacker' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Other Life</a> and even the one I was sure would be the exception to the rule - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8051458.The_Reapers_Are_the_Angels' title='The Reapers Are the Angels by Alden Bell' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Reapers Are the Angels</a>, and that is that zombie novels have never been my thin</span>
  <span id="freeText5370463818902947329" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4.5</b><br><br>I owe a huge thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> for giving me a second chance to read and review this after my netgalley rejection. It made my day and I'm so glad <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_Is_Not_a_Test" title="This Is Not a Test by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Not a Test</a> was all that I'd hoped it would be.<br><br>I'm going to say what I said at the start of my reviews or before I started reading: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7094569.Feed__Newsflesh_Trilogy__1_" title="Feed (Newsflesh Trilogy #1) by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Feed</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9554790.The_Other_Life__The_Other_Life___1_" title="The Other Life (The Other Life, #1) by Susanne Winnacker" rel="nofollow noopener">The Other Life</a> and even the one I was sure would be the exception to the rule - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8051458.The_Reapers_Are_the_Angels" title="The Reapers Are the Angels by Alden Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">The Reapers Are the Angels</a>, and that is that zombie novels have never been my thing. I've searched and searched for that one book that would allow me to share in my friends' love for novels of the walking dead, brain-eating variety. This is the first - yes, the very first - book about zombies I have enjoyed. Ah, but then I suppose this isn't really <i>that much</i> about zombies.<br><br>As with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>' other novels, this is mostly a book about people, about survival. Summers does survival tales best, it doesn't matter whether the threat is zombies, grief or a bunch of bitchy teenage girls, every situation is equally poignant and Summers never fails to leave a lasting impression. <br><br>This is the tale of a group of teenagers who barricade themselves into what was once their high school as the zombie apocalypse descends outside. Each character has something important to offer this novel and, for me, when you can make this kind of statement it puts <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> up their with the few others who have this rare talent - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a>, to name a couple. And on top of that, they all have a story, they are all fighting something that goes beyond the realm of living corpses, and this is what I like most about this novel. In most zombie stories, people fight until they die and maybe one or two survive... but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> remembers that, even in the apocalypse, living is about more than just not getting eaten and perhaps sometimes there are scarier things out there than those zombies, and even death.<br><br>Also, it is worth noting, I have always said that zombies do not scare me at all. When watching horror films, if zombies manage to get any kind of reaction from me it's usually amusement at their silly moans. But this was one hell of a creepy novel. I'm not sure why this book managed to give me chills when so many others failed, but I admit it, I was freaked out, and not always at the zombies.<br><br>My only criticism will not be a problem for some people. In fact, you may find it positive. Summers' endings are always sharp, brutal, effective but sometimes a little too abrupt for me. The ending to this will leave you thinking, wondering... you will undoubtedly be affected by it. But, for me, there was a lack of closure that I felt I needed from a novel I'd become so emotionally invested in. Otherwise, this was a fantastic novel and I knew <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> wouldn't let me down. I will read everything she writes, no question.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5370463818902947329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_266793140" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266793140" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266793140?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266793140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18061699391066264507">[<i>Edited, because ZOMBIE NAILS. See below</i>]<br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><s>This is not a zombie book. </s><br/><br/>This book <i>has</i> zombies in it. But it’s not <i>about</i> zombies, as such.<br/><br/>It’s about so much more than that.<br/><br/>Call them a catalyst, a threat, an inciting event – the zombies are an ominous presence that set off a chain reaction of events and lurk unnervingly around the corners of the book. But this is not even so much a book about survival, although that’s certainly one of the themes threading through the story. <br/><br/>For me, deep at it</span>
  <span id="freeText18061699391066264507" style="display:none">[<i>Edited, because ZOMBIE NAILS. See below</i>]<br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><s>This is not a zombie book. </s><br><br>This book <i>has</i> zombies in it. But it’s not <i>about</i> zombies, as such.<br><br>It’s about so much more than that.<br><br>Call them a catalyst, a threat, an inciting event – the zombies are an ominous presence that set off a chain reaction of events and lurk unnervingly around the corners of the book. But this is not even so much a book about survival, although that’s certainly one of the themes threading through the story. <br><br>For me, deep at its heart, this was a book about <i>will</i>. The will to live versus the will to die. And how sometimes, for some people, this is not an unconscious, involuntary response to each day as it arrives, but a choice and a fight every moment.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_is_Not_a_Test" title="This is Not a Test by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Not A Test</a> is an incredibly intense and psychologically gruelling novel to read. It had me in a stranglehold from the first page, from Sloane’s opening words, which almost echo with the emptiness carved out by her sister's absence. While her pain bleeds through the pages in places, there’s also something detached, cold, about her narration. Because her mind has been made up. She’s resolved. Until the morning the world shatters.<br><br>In depicting her vision of the zombie apocalypse, Summers uses restraint to masterful effect. The horror of the undead is rendered more powerful by the <i>suggestion</i> of their presence, like the sound of them hammering against doors in their hunger, as opposed to always placing them in the limelight. Similarly, by barricading six teenagers into a school, it’s the constant fear of a breach that stretches the nerves to breaking point, rather than an endless gore-fest. Which is not to say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_is_Not_a_Test" title="This is Not a Test by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Not A Test</a> doesn’t contain disturbing images of violence or pay homage to the genre of zombie horror – it does – but the effectiveness is amplified by the enormous amount of tension that has been wound up in the plot.<br><br>The scenario of six people thrown together, under siege by the rabid infected and forced to make snap judgements with life or death ramifications, makes for a mental battleground. The dynamic balances on a knife-edge, allegiances and motivations threatened by accusations, guilt and desperation born out of the desire to live (or die). At work beneath the more obvious conflicts are the character’s own internal battles, and the larger questions of what it means to take or save a life, and at what cost do they preserve their own. Who is the real enemy - the undead, or the darker side of human nature?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_is_Not_a_Test" title="This is Not a Test by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Not A Test</a> almost defies categorisation. It’s a hybrid of sorts, and the brutal emotional honesty is not sacrificed in order to continue ratcheting up the tension. It sounds strange, but the juxtaposition of the contemporary elements with the horror premise work exceptionally well. The parallels between the internal and external fight to survive are powerful, and there is a depth and relevance to this story in it’s insightful portrayal of pain, loss, grief, and ultimately, choice. <br><br>In Sloane, Summers has created a character and a story that hit me right in the chest. I felt an almost relentless ache for her, for what had compelled her to make her decision. And yet never does the writing feel gratuitous or melodramatic. It feels painfully realistic, all the more powerful for the things that are left unspoken, the profound silences between the scenes. <br><br>I was exhausted when I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_is_Not_a_Test" title="This is Not a Test by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Not A Test</a>. I felt mentally, emotionally, physically (because I stayed up so late to read it) wrung out – and the haunting final scene of the book lingered with me days afterwards. <br><br>I’m a little bit in awe of this book. <br><br>And I’m going to start sleeping with a cricket bat under my bed. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368133i/720636.jpg" width="300" alt="tinat1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368133i/720637.jpg" width="300" alt="tinat" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18061699391066264507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_212256641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/212256641" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/212256641?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212256641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12410565926362102760">When someone sees a zombie book there are two reactions: 1) Oh zombies, scary and gory! AwesomeSAUCE! or 2) Ewww zombies! Icky! - pass. So this is a warning: As far as zombie books go, This Is Not A Test has to be one of the tamest. It's not gory, nor is it an adrenaline filled story. Yes there are zombies and it can get intense at times, but funnily enough, it is <u>not</u> about the zombies. It's about a girl who doesn't want to live in this world anymore. She can't keep going with a dad that beats h</span>
  <span id="freeText12410565926362102760" style="display:none">When someone sees a zombie book there are two reactions: 1) Oh zombies, scary and gory! AwesomeSAUCE! or 2) Ewww zombies! Icky! - pass. So this is a warning: As far as zombie books go, This Is Not A Test has to be one of the tamest. It's not gory, nor is it an adrenaline filled story. Yes there are zombies and it can get intense at times, but funnily enough, it is <u>not</u> about the zombies. It's about a girl who doesn't want to live in this world anymore. She can't keep going with a dad that beats her, and a sister that left her. This book is about finding the will to live in all this melancholy. Surviving in a school with others who only want to make it through this zombocalypse, when all Sloane wants to do is leave. To let the zombies take her away from this unforgiving world. <br><br>Even though the zombies almost never make an appearance. It doesn't mean it's not frightening. Courtney weaves them in the always present background; leaving them to our imagination makes them scary in a way no one else can. We don't know what's happening on the outside and with a constant fear of breach, the tension in the story is unmistakable. The unknown is a terrifying illusion. This is the angle Courtney takes to make this book absolutely unnerving.<br><br>With half a dozen teenagers in a life or death situation, there is no absence of angst. However, it's not aggravating, it's realism. It was written with such authenticity that you never feel annoyance, only distress. These are not just surface characters, either. This is a gang of teenagers who are experiencing the end of the world; who have lost everyone they ever knew and loved; who just want to make it through to the next day without killing each other - or dying at the hands of the zombies. We get to know these characters to the core, exposed. We see them at their most vulnerable. It's all so raw that you get to care deeply for these people. Even when you're not reading, you're constantly worrying about them; it's mentally exhausting, but truly captivating. These personalities who often clash have to learn to work together if they want to come out of this alive. It's sad, it's heartbreaking, and there's a constant sense of doom in the air. One positive vibe throughout, though, is the hope. These kids make the best of what they have, and you always feel like somehow, things will work out.<br><br>This story is one that sticks with you, with an ending that leaves you in a bittersweet mess where you're not sure if you should cry, or simply exhale and let it go. This was my first novel by Courtney Summers, but if this is an example of her writing, I can say she has exceptional talent that I will seek out again with immense anticipation.<br><br>--<br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358334i/709537.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1124624084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124624084" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1124624084?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Marchetta's fans :)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup">epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=unexpected-but-awesome">unexpected-but-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124624084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10284869788878263662"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423513440i/13636672._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>2015 reads</u> : <s>Do not</s> give me zombies, 'kay?</b><br/><br/>▨ <b>This is not a book <i>about</i> zombies, this is a book <i>with</i> zombies.</b><br/><br/><b>And I'm so okay with that</b>. I mean, to be frank, I'm not into zombies. Like, at all. Usually, they never manage to : <br/><i>a) Scare me<br/>b) Interest me</i><br/>Dead people who come back to life? Come on! That's just gross to me. Therefore I end bored more often than not, except if I take it as a parody, changing myself into this annoying buddy who can't help but laugh at awkward moments (sorry guys for all the</span>
  <span id="freeText10284869788878263662" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423513440i/13636672._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>2015 reads</u> : <s>Do not</s> give me zombies, 'kay?</b><br><br>▨ <b>This is not a book <i>about</i> zombies, this is a book <i>with</i> zombies.</b><br><br><b>And I'm so okay with that</b>. I mean, to be frank, I'm not into zombies. Like, at all. Usually, they never manage to : <br><i>a) Scare me<br>b) Interest me</i><br>Dead people who come back to life? Come on! That's just gross to me. Therefore I end bored more often than not, except if I take it as a parody, changing myself into this annoying buddy who can't help but laugh at awkward moments (sorry guys for all the movies I ruined). If it wasn't for all the reviews I read which pointed that it wasn't really a zombie horror book, I'd probably never have given it a chance. That's why I'm pointing it too : <b>If you expect a classic horror story, you'll be disappointed</b>. <br><br>▨ <b>This is not a book where the <i>zombies</i> scare you, this is a book where the <i>characters</i> make you think.</b> <br><br>Now, you know I'm a huge fan girl when it comes to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a>, especially because I can't help but fall in love with every single character she brings to life. <b>In this book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> manages to create flawed characters I adore.</b> Though it was anything but evident at first, because I have a thing : I don't usually love depressive characters. Yeah, you got it, the key word here is <i>usually</i>. Indeed <b>Sloane</b> is all kind of depressing - she actually <i>wants</i> to die - and yet she managed to move me like crazy. How did she do this? <i>How?</i> I'm not sure I can't even explain. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"We'll become reanimated corpses navigating a sorry imitation of our glory days and this is why I don't understand the point in going on, why it's so wrong to give up. There's nothing left."</b>
</blockquote><br>There's something so <i>desperate</i> in her way to handle all the crazy stuff that happens constantly and yet she's never <i>ever</i> whining. Not a single time - I often found myself in awe of her perseverance, as I think there's some braveness to show such motivation, even if it's to <i>die</i> at some point. <i>Did I find it stupid?</i> <b>Of course I did</b>. I have a thing against suicide, I can't deny it, that's totally personal and I can't help it - it often obscures my judgment about characters like her, because not only suicide makes me sad, but it <b>piss me off</b>. <b>But</b> Sloane won me. Completely. I took her with all her flaws and wanted just one thing : to read about her. <br><br>➸ Look, I'm not saying she's going to die. In fact, I'm not saying anything - she's a believable character you know, so <b>she can evolve. Or not</b>. <i>Yep, I'm totally a tease.</i><br><br>▨ <b>This is not a book about <i>battles</i>, this is a book about <i>survival</i> and all we're ready to do to survive.</b><br><br><i>because...</i><br><br>▨ <b>This is not a book filled with <i>teenage angst</i>, this is a book about the <i>inherent injustice of life</i>.</b> <br><br><b>What do you think you'd be willing to do to survive?</b> As I already said in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6043849.The_Ask_and_the_Answer__Chaos_Walking___2_" title="The Ask and the Answer (Chaos Walking, #2) by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ask and the Answer</a>, the only honest answer I can give you is <i>I don't know</i>. Sure, I could convince myself that I wouldn't be selfish and would always do the <i>right</i> thing but <b>we have to know what this right thing is to begin with</b>. Is it saving your parents? Saving your love? Saving yourself? Saving the human race? Tell me when you find your answer because I'm not sure I'll manage to. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"It was so easy," he said. "Just physically ... doing that. When it was over, I thought ... people ... we aren't made of anything. That's how easy it was."</b>
</blockquote><br>Each character has his choices to make, and what can I say? That's <i>real</i>, that's <i>painful</i>, that made me <i>feel</i> : I can't <b>not</b> love it. <br><br>▨ <b>This is not a book you'll spend <i>days</i> to read, this is a book you're going to eat in <i>one sitting</i>.</b><br><br><u>Surely you know the feeling</u> : you're reading a book, sure that you've reached 50%, and you're stunned to realize that in fact you're at, like, 15%. <b>This book brings the exact opposite of that feeling.</b> Although the writing can appear pretty confusing in the beginning, <b>I was hooked from page one and this feeling never ended until the end</b>. Indeed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>'s writing contains particularities that I never fail to love when I'm lucky to find them : short and sharp sentences, well-done repetitions - her style completely serves the plot as it helps grandly to express the <b>growing tension</b> the characters feel. <br><br>▨ <b>This is not a review, this is ... well, if this is not a review, I have no idea what the fuck it is.</b> <br><br><u>PS</u> : I thought I wasn't scared and in the end, it seems that the sensation of being threatened grew on me without realizing it. <i>Yes, I totally freaked out when I got out to let my dog pee. Poor me.</i><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="10284869788878263662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_267111048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267111048" />
    <a title="Megs ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5691412-megs"><img alt="Megs ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587306329p2/5691412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267111048?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megs ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megs ♥" href="/user/show/5691412-megs">Megs ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2012-reads">z-2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=cover-lover">cover-lover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=favs">favs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267111048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8046912640921938242">This has been said a few times, but it's certainly worth repeating. This is not really a zombie book. Although it has zombies in it, they are just the constant threat in the book, and they are minimally shown. The gore is quite minimal, too. This is just a warning for others, like myself, who aren't really into gory books, because I wouldn't want anyone to not read this book just because of that. Of course that can go both ways, however, and a zombie fan looking for an all out gore-fest may be d</span>
  <span id="freeText8046912640921938242" style="display:none">This has been said a few times, but it's certainly worth repeating. This is not really a zombie book. Although it has zombies in it, they are just the constant threat in the book, and they are minimally shown. The gore is quite minimal, too. This is just a warning for others, like myself, who aren't really into gory books, because I wouldn't want anyone to not read this book just because of that. Of course that can go both ways, however, and a zombie fan looking for an all out gore-fest may be disappointed.<br /><br />After I read the opening chapter of this book I was blown away. It was quite intense. We are introduced to our main character, Sloane, who has just been and frequently is physically abused by her father. Suddenly there is a woman pounding on their door, and she's covered in blood. Her father finds out that their street is full of screaming and chaos, and then quickly the scene switches to Sloane in the High School with 5 other students. Six survivors after the zombie apocalypse. They have barricaded the windows and doors. They have food,water, and a radio to listen for emergency broadcasts. All they can do now is wait for help to arrive.<br /><br />This story has a lot going on for how short it is, but it never feels cluttered. We know that Sloane was abandoned by her sister, Lily, but the details of what was supposed to happen and how that has affected her come out slowly throughout the book. The main focus of this book is each person's will to live. Lily was all Sloane had left so once she left her she has none. Sloane wants desperately to just die. I thought the author wrote this very well. We can feel Sloane's desperation and hopelessness, but she never seems emo.<br /><br />Each of the students has a very different personality, and they need to learn to work together, despite their disagreements, if they want to survive. With a book about six teens I often find myself getting really annoyed with about half of them, because of their attitudes. This didn't happen with this book, luckily. At one point I was starting to get annoyed with Trace and his bossiness, but that was just his personality and it wasn't overdone. These kids all lost everything and almost everyone they loved. I felt bad for them, yet hopeful they would survive.<br /><br />The last chapter was just as intense as the first. I was feverishly turning the pages wanting to know what was going to happen next. This chapter was action packed and seemed to fly by so quickly my head was spinning at the end. I am so happy about Sloane's personal ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The Sloane we met in the beginning was definitely not the same Sloane was got at the end. Courtney did an amazing job with writing her character, and the growth she experienced throughout this book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I absolutely loved this book. I read it in one sitting, and only had one complaint. I wish we would have seen a little more of the intensity like the first and last chapters throughout the book. I knew that at any point zombies could get into the building, but I never really felt scared for the characters while they were in the school. I also knew that at any point Sloane could be simply bitten once to end her life, but again I never felt like that would happen. Those are just my feelings, though, and I could easily see this book being a solid 5-star book for many other readers.<br /><br />This was my first book by Courtney Summers, but I will definitely be checking out more of her books. I was really impressed with this one. <br /><br />4.5/5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8046912640921938242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_225793295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225793295" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225793295?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225793295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3101068889079017219">4 1/2 stars<br/><br/>Because I’m a fancy <i>creative post</i> writer, I thought I’d start this off with a quote from someone whose opinion I really trust:<br/><br/>“<i>Can you imagine what she's going to do with zombie survival?!! I bet it's going to be gruesome. :D</i>”<br/><br/>You know what? I really do love the sound of my own voice. You are so, so right, me of approximately five months ago.<br/><br/>Of course, this is Courtney Summers so the “gruesome” part of this book doesn’t arrive with the zombie apocalypse; it takes place within the grasp</span>
  <span id="freeText3101068889079017219" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars<br /><br />Because I’m a fancy <i>creative post</i> writer, I thought I’d start this off with a quote from someone whose opinion I really trust:<br /><br />“<i>Can you imagine what she's going to do with zombie survival?!! I bet it's going to be gruesome. :D</i>”<br /><br />You know what? I really do love the sound of my own voice. You are so, so right, me of approximately five months ago.<br /><br />Of course, this is Courtney Summers so the “gruesome” part of this book doesn’t arrive with the zombie apocalypse; it takes place within the grasping, desperate, damaged minds of the survivors. Which I think is a common thread in all the best zombie novels, really. Zombies are compelling in that they speak to some of our deepest fears; for example, that our bodies could become vacant killing machines, piloted by something other than ourselves. It’s a complete loss of free will. But in some sense, zombies can easily be a stand-in for any mass disaster or plague. What’s most compelling is the reaction of the human survivors <i>to</i> the zombies.<br /><br />This book has one of the best opening chapters I’ve read in a really long time. It is completely subtle but also utterly horrifying and absorbing. We are introduced to the main character Sloane in one brief, emotionally intense snapshot. Her life is a confining, meaningless misery and now that her sister is gone, she doesn’t see the point in continuing. She’s just about to finally let go when something happens – a shattering window, a crazed woman, a mad rush of humanity outside. And then we are pushed forward in time by seven days, as Sloane and five other survivors find shelter in their high school. What happened in those seven days was ugly and brutal, but we are not shown the details fully. We are given a front row seat to the more interesting part – the aftermath. <br /> <br />I’ve long admired Courtney Summers’ writing, because she really has a talent for getting in deep with the darker emotions and portraying them with such stark honesty that it’s impossible not to be affected. But in this book I feel like she’s really grown as a writer, finding that perfect balance between subtlety and story-telling. She hits us with bright pieces of emotion and action, but she never fills in <i>all</i> the blanks. It's subtle but evocative enough that we are compelled to contribute – we have to put ourselves into the story. She can lead us down the path, but we have to use our own emotions and experiences to make the final steps. I think that’s one of the hallmarks of a great writer – because in the end, no writer can complete a story alone. No writer can describe an emotion with such perfection that someone who’s never felt it before will suddenly understand it. The best writers lead us to our own emotions, and the best stories are collaborations between writers <i>and</i> readers. I think that Courtney Summers really masters that with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_Is_Not_a_Test" title="This Is Not a Test by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Not a Test</a>.<br /><br />And of course, this woman writes my favorite kind of endings – dark but ambiguously hopeful, with realistic growth in the main character – perfection. <br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Florence + The Machine – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=l78ZE9hjjzE" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Let Me Go</a><br /><br />That’s right, I’m pulling out all the stops for this book! No less than Florence will do. This song, to me, is about giving up on everything, completely, only to realize that you’ve survived anyway. <br /><br />And now I need to make an announcement. Attention everyone: this is not a test. Go crazy for this book. Bloggers: it’s time to light up the super special ARC signal in the sky. Courtney Summers fans: do whatever you have to do - crack each other’s heads open and feast on the goo inside if you must. Just get this book. This is not a test people!<br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/04/ya-review-this-is-not-a-test-by-courtney-summers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3101068889079017219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397502811" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4336740206305936450">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>3.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"This must be what Dorothy felt like, I think. Maybe. If Dorothy was six scared teenagers and Oz was hell."</i>
</b><br/><br/>When I saw ALLLLLLL of my friends reading <i>All the Rage</i> recently I figured I would end up reading it wrong (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391902659?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Exhibit A</a>) and opted for Summers’ version of zombies instead . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442853323ra/16284985.gif' alt='Chicago commercial photographers' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>What can I say? I’m not interested in being the oddball again this week but I enjoy brain-nomming stories. *shrug*<br/><br/>However, being that Sum</span>
  <span id="freeText4336740206305936450" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>3.5 Stars<br><br><b>
  <i>"This must be what Dorothy felt like, I think. Maybe. If Dorothy was six scared teenagers and Oz was hell."</i>
</b><br><br>When I saw ALLLLLLL of my friends reading <i>All the Rage</i> recently I figured I would end up reading it wrong (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391902659?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Exhibit A</a>) and opted for Summers’ version of zombies instead . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442853323ra/16284985.gif" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What can I say? I’m not interested in being the oddball again this week but I enjoy brain-nomming stories. *shrug*<br><br>However, being that Summers is Summers, this book had a lot less of this . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>The premise seemed familiar – the zombie apocalypse began a week ago, leaving <s>a brain, an athlete, a basket case, a princess, and a criminal</s> six students no choice but to work together in hopes of surviving the danger that potentially lurks around every corner of their former high school where they are holed up . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/illinois/chicago/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442853323ra/16284988.gif" alt="Chicago commercial photographers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

</a><br><br><b>*DUN DUN DUNNNNNNNNN*</b><br><br>Okay, so while the basic concept has been done a time or twelve before the delivery was 100% unique. If <i>Lord of the Flies</i> and <i>The Walking Dead</i> had a baby you might end up with something along the lines of <i>This Is Not A Test</i>. If you like your zombies with a lot of gore and a high body count you should probably look elsewhere. On the other hand, if you’re looking for a “zombie” book that deals more with questions of mortality and morality, this is the book for you. Summers is quickly becoming a YA fave.<br><br></span>

<div id="review_1230563165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230563165" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230563165?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230563165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4900552732943932074"><br/><b> <i> "Now is not about gathering courage, it's about staying one step ahead of my fear." </i></b> <br/> <br/>Oh my goodness gracious! What did I just read???<br/> <br/>I have this basic concept about how any story that has to do with zombies is old and funny. Sorry I don’t watch Walking Dead.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426820898ra/14100773.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>But I am now completely eradicating that concept from my mind because of this dark but masterfully written prose.<br/> <br/>This is my first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers' title='Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Summers</a> read and I am instantly and immediately captivated by the unique writing style via her us</span>
  <span id="freeText4900552732943932074" style="display:none"><br><b> <i> "Now is not about gathering courage, it's about staying one step ahead of my fear." </i></b> <br> <br>Oh my goodness gracious! What did I just read???<br> <br>I have this basic concept about how any story that has to do with zombies is old and funny. Sorry I don’t watch Walking Dead.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426820898ra/14100773.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>But I am now completely eradicating that concept from my mind because of this dark but masterfully written prose.<br> <br>This is my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> read and I am instantly and immediately captivated by the unique writing style via her use of first person narrative voice in the character of Sloane, a teenage girl who has lost the will to live but unexplainably finds herself struggling to survive alongside five other teenagers after the end of the world strikes and dead people turn into reanimated corpses who are set on multiplying their numbers by feasting on the living to eventually become like them.<br> <br>The plot starts a little slow as it establishes the major characters and their specific roles in putting across the themes of the story. Every character represents the obvious but very convincing possibilities of human nature when faced with existential crisis. The heated dialogues, the impossible choices they had to make, the way they had to live which can be barely called living, the urge to do and feel things they think they might never be able to tomorrow, holding out waiting for nothing because nothing happens. It all felt real and made this a very gripping and powerful story and you find yourself immersed in their grim situation.<br> <br>It’s very impressive because from parts one to three, the author created only one focal setting- the school, but she managed to make the reader imagine a decaying world infested with flesh eating living dead outside the school. What’s even more impressive is how the author purposefully subdued the events during the first parts of the story because she was saving shocking surprises during the fourth part where a hailstorm of crazy $#1% happens. Initially, I was adamant in saying.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423737621ra/13664990.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>I shouldn’t be. Why should I? They’re just zombies. But the truth is, I was terrified! How did the author manage to do that???<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381732862ra/5247119.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>I was so disgusted at the gruesome deaths because of the vividly horrid descriptions.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426748034ra/14088937.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Also, I was horribly shocked at that sick twist of events towards the ending…<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392903276ra/8630384.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>and I was left hanging at the end. Yes, it was a cliffhanger ending that will make you want to scream and go crazy in your need to get your hands on the sequel!<br> <br>This wasn’t a perfect post apocalyptic novel but the provocative prose will make you forget about the imperfections. This is a must read.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4900552732943932074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_379134916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379134916" />
    <a title="Wigs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4719641-wigs"><img alt="Wigs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327112868p2/4719641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379134916?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wigs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wigs" href="/user/show/4719641-wigs">Wigs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379134916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5072502484270448085">This is Not a Good Book.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385666ra/744715.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The summary sounded good. Six teens trapped in a school during a zombie crisis slowly go nuts on each other. The book did not deliver. What I was imagining from the summary was some sort of manhunt dog-eat-dog Lord of the Flies style breaking down of these trapped teenagers, where basic survival instincts would drive them into some crazy game of hide and seek trying to kill each other. In essence, the group of survivors themselves would be a more dangerous enemy to each o</span>
  <span id="freeText5072502484270448085" style="display:none">This is Not a Good Book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385666ra/744715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The summary sounded good. Six teens trapped in a school during a zombie crisis slowly go nuts on each other. The book did not deliver. What I was imagining from the summary was some sort of manhunt dog-eat-dog Lord of the Flies style breaking down of these trapped teenagers, where basic survival instincts would drive them into some crazy game of hide and seek trying to kill each other. In essence, the group of survivors themselves would be a more dangerous enemy to each other than any zombie could be.<br><br>Well.<br><br>What I got was just a group of whiny regular teens emoing it up. Acting like idiots. Whining. Wandering around. Taking showers. Crying. Ugh. The tediousness of this book seems never ending. The main character Sloane, who narrates in a thoroughly obnoxious, sparsely descriptive first person present tense, is suicidal. She spends the entire book up to like the last few pages wanting to die and it just really gets old. If I had to hear about her sister ~leaving~ her behind one more time...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385666ra/744716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's fine to set up the plot but just please stop going on and on and on and on and on and onnnnnn about it. And not only that, but all conversations from all the characters felt repetitive. The same shit kept coming up. "You killed our parents." "No I didn't." "Your fault." "No." "But it is your fault!" "It's not!" Over and over. Just stopppppp. Everyone was just so stupid and one dimensional. <br><br>The entire book could be probably condensed to a quarter of its length if you trimmed out all the stuff we hear multiple times over. And so much shoe leather! I walked down the hall I went upstairs I went back to the auditorium I went to the gym I went to the bathroom GREAT but you never do anything so why are you telling us all this useless stuff. <br><br>Sorry. I feel boring just talking about it.<br><br>Oh, and author, please. Please. Do not name, out of 6 characters in the entire book, one of them Grace and another Trace. I don't care if they're siblings, please choose another name that isn't the exact same thing. Seeing Grace Trace Grace Trace Grace Trace all down the page....well actually it's possibly symbolic of how redundant this book is.<br><br>At the end, things kinda picked up a little bit, some zombie action and stuff that happens, finally, outside the damn school. In the very. last. 10% of the book. That does not excuse the rest, and the ending which is supposed to be a surprise I suppose was predictable and lackluster. The resolution final page barely made sense, with some not very well constructed metaphor that just left me going ehhhh what? <br><br>Okay.<br><br>I apologize. This is a lot of ranting. The point is, I was bored to tears most of the time and the only reason why I finish stuff like this is because I want another notch on my books read in 2012 badge. <br><br>#gurlbye<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5072502484270448085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235469487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235469487" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235469487?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235469487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6725807809727420645"><b>
  <i>"…I think it isn’t enough to survive for the sake of surviving…. Surviving should mean something like it means something to them. And if it doesn’t-<br/>If it doesn’t."</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b><s>Initial Final Page Thoughts. </s> <br/><br/>An Exchange of E-Mails between a friend and I. </b><br/>[Censored for spoilery badtimes]<br/><br/><b><u>Last night.</u><br/>10.49 pm.</b><br/>OMG THIS BOOK.<br/>THIS IS A BOOK THAT NEEDS TO BE TALKED ABOUT IN CAPITAL LETTERS.<br/><br/><b>[blank]</b> and then <b>[blank]</b> and omg <b>[blank]</b> !!!<br/><br/>OMG CATIE. WHAT.... WHAT.... *head implodes*<br/><br/><b>11.06pm.</b><br/>[<i>A reply from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1886642-catie' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catie</a>, aka, Pres</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6725807809727420645" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"…I think it isn’t enough to survive for the sake of surviving…. Surviving should mean something like it means something to them. And if it doesn’t-<br />If it doesn’t."</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b><s>Initial Final Page Thoughts. </s> <br /><br />An Exchange of E-Mails between a friend and I. </b><br />[Censored for spoilery badtimes]<br /><br /><b><u>Last night.</u><br />10.49 pm.</b><br />OMG THIS BOOK.<br />THIS IS A BOOK THAT NEEDS TO BE TALKED ABOUT IN CAPITAL LETTERS.<br /><br /><b>[blank]</b> and then <b>[blank]</b> and omg <b>[blank]</b> !!!<br /><br />OMG CATIE. WHAT.... WHAT.... *head implodes*<br /><br /><b>11.06pm.</b><br />[<i>A reply from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1886642-catie" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Catie</a>, aka, President of Courtney Summers' Fan Club</i>.]<br />THIS BOOK. The title just kept passing through my head - THIS IS NOT A TEST. Too<b> [blank]</b>ing right it's not! She really pulled out all the stops I think. Her best.<br /><br /><b>11:20 pm. </b><br />CATIE. A chav just threw a snowball at my window and I swear I literally just died for a split second.<br /><br /><b>11.31 pm.</b><br />OMG WHEN HE <b>[blank]</b>. OMG I can’t even deal with this book now. I’ve actually had to stop reading for the night to calm down.<br />Blarrgh. <br /><br /><b><u>Next day.</u><br />11.45 am</b><br />[<i>Shh, I had a lie in. It was Sunday!</i>]<br />I hope <b>[blank]</b> doesn’t turn into a baddie. Or a zombie. Or a zombaddie.<br /><br /><b>11.48 am.</b><br />A <b>[blank]</b>?!?! OH COME ON *gnaws off hand*<br /><br /><b>11.55 am.</b><br />[<i>At this point punctuation, never a strong point of mine, failed me completely</i>.]<br />the <b>[blank] </b>??? !!!! omg what is with courtney summers she is an evil evil GENIUS woman<br /><br /><b>12.08pm.</b><br />IS <b>[blank]</b> GOING TO BE A <b>[blank]</b>?!?!<br />Don’t tell me.<br />I don’t want to know.<br />UNLESS <b>[blank]</b> and then they <b>[blank] </b>and then omg<b> [blank] and [blank].</b><br />no… still don’t tell me. <br /><br /><b>12.22pm.</b><br />OMFG.<br />Are you kidding me?!<br />ARE YOU ACTUALLY KIDDING ME?!<br /><br /><b>12.37pm</b><br />[<i>When I reached the end. Censored for my language because I could make a sailor blush with my muck mouth</i>.]<br />Holy <b>[blank]</b>-a-doodle-do.<br /><br />The above should give you an insight on what this review is going to be like.<br />Manic? Possibly. <br />Gushing? Probably. <br />Incoherent? Pffft… you know me too well. ;-) <br />Let’s just call it passionate, shall we?<br />The above should also give you an insight on how <i>brilliant</i> it is to get an e-mail off me. <br /><br /><b>High Points. </b><br />In a perfect world. Survivors. Lockers. Notes. Sisters. Family. Pressure. <i>“drenched in someone else’s life.”</i> Book bags. Broken. Tina T. <i>”Thud.”</i>. Saying good-bye. Safety in numbers. Bait. What comes next?<br /><br /><b>Low Points.</b><br />Trace and Grace…. Really? Are any parents that cruel?! <br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />Sloane… crimeny.<br /><br /><i>“I’m lying because I’m the only one that can say the things I need to hear.”</i><br /><br />Ms Summers sure knows how to create a broken heroine, doesn’t she?<br /><br /><i>“I’m just waiting for the rest of me to catch up.”</i><br /><br />Gah.<br /><br /><b>Supporting Cast.</b><br />OMG <b>[blank]</b> AND WHEN THEY WERE IN THE <b>[blank]</b> and OMG <b>[blank]</b> OMG WHY DID <b>[blank]</b> JUST DO THAT?!?!?!<br />Guh.<br />The interactions between these characters in that last part? <br />Literally made my mind implode.<br />LITERALLY.<br /><br />....<br /><br />OK, maybe not <i>literally.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br />Seeing as I was still jibbering at the end of this book, I asked Catie to help me pick out a song for this book.<br />I needed one bleak and horrifying and poignant and remarkably human. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nZq_jeYsbTs" rel="nofollow noopener">How to Disappear Completely- Radiohead.</a> <br /><br /><i>Strobe lights and broken speakers<br />Fireworks and hurricanes<br />I’m not here.<br />This isn’t happening<br />I’m not here.<br />I’m not here. </i><br /><br />*shivers*<br /><br /><b><s>Sadness Scale</s> OMFG Scale</b><br />I made two cups of tea while I was reading this book and both of them went cold.<br />The moral of this story?<br />Drink juice when reading Ms Summers.<br />Or, like, a milkshake or something. <br /><br />You know that bit in a horror film when you see a shadow flick across the screen behind the doe-eyed heroine? And there’s the feeling in your stomach where you know terrible things are going to happen but you just don’t know when?<br />Ms Summers has turned that feeling into a book and that book is called ‘This is Not a Test’. <br /><br />I think people who go into this book expecting it to be a zombook (“<i>Braaaaains</i>”) will be incredibly disappointed. <br />Because, to me, this isn’t a zombie book.<br />This book is a snapshot into suffering and despair and humanity and it’s one that’s blown up to such high-definition that it’s difficult to stomach because it’s honest and it’s brutal and it’s real and it’s so intense in its depiction of unbearable human emotions that you just want to gnaw on a pillow and curl up in the foetal position. <br /><br />Also, there are zombies. <br />Zombies that eat <i>braaaaaains</i>.<br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who are ready to join the land of the living. People who are compelled to chase their nightmares. People who wonder what astronauts do when a zombie outbreak breaks…out. People who wonder what celebrities do in a zombie outbreak (Seriously Courtney Summers, get out of my mind! I always think of stuff like that!). People who wonder whether the zombies are the ones they should be worried about. People who could wield a crowbar without hitting themselves in the face with it. People who would stay on the side of zombie-infested side of the fence with me when they realise there is no chance in hell I’m going to be able to get over that because my upper body strength is non-existent. I mean we could <i>try</i> and find a loose slat or something but I might as well apologise to you now in the off-chance we find ourselves in that situation. <br /><br /><i>I received an advanced copy from the publishers. </i><br /><br /></span>
