<span id="freeTextContainer16397060527005223878">It only took me a few pages to remember how much I love Summers' unique style of writing: punchy, direct, achey, intense. Minimal words conveying maximum impact.<br/><br/>It took me only one chapter to be hooked. By the end of chapter one, I needed to read chapter two. By the end of chapter two, I needed to read chapter three. By the end of … and so on.<br/><br/>This is Not a Test is compulsively readable. Tightly plotted. Intense. Addictive. The drama in the pages never seems melodramatic, in spite of the premise.</span>
  <span id="freeText16397060527005223878" style="display:none">It only took me a few pages to remember how much I love Summers' unique style of writing: punchy, direct, achey, intense. Minimal words conveying maximum impact.<br /><br />It took me only one chapter to be hooked. By the end of chapter one, I needed to read chapter two. By the end of chapter two, I needed to read chapter three. By the end of … and so on.<br /><br />This is Not a Test is compulsively readable. Tightly plotted. Intense. Addictive. The drama in the pages never seems melodramatic, in spite of the premise. <br /><br />I didn't find it had a breakfast club vibe at all: to me, that implies misfits ultimately banding together. Which didn't happen. Tensions ran high and then they ran higher.<br /><br />What I loved about this book was how sucked in I got. Made an awesome reading experience. I truly love courtney summers for that. <br /><br />However, I was ultimately unsatisfied. I didn’t really connect to the characters. I was curious about what would go down, but not affected by any of it. I felt very disconnected to Sloane, who is disconnected to herself in many ways. Sloane is just as messed up (if not more) than any other of summers protagonists: abused, broken, closed-up, suicidal, distanced from other characters.<br /><br />The last 20% was my least favourite part. When everything started to fall apart, I inexplicably felt tired of the drama.<br /><br />The ending, for me, was the worst, although not unexpected. I am just not sure how I am supposed to feel about the book being left there. It was harsh. Instead of finishing the book on the adrenalin rush of the first sections, i was stunned, disheartened and oddly, empty. Dazed. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I did not like the ending with Lily and Sloane's father. I mean, why? What should readers take form that? After all the build-up and hearing about Lily the whole novel. Why even bring her back, to finish her off, off page. I think I missed the lesson/theme/whatever there. Also, Sloane and Rhys together at the end, just the two of them wandering off. is this the hopeful note?. I don't know. I wasn't very invested in their relationship either, not as love interests, but even as friends. Hmm...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Regarding the zombies: It read much more like a contemp novel, really. However, the action and gore scenes were great and obviously provided a unique environment/background for Sloane’s internal drama. <br /><br />Recommended: Definitely for an engrossing, addictive, original read, This Is Not A Test is the book you’re looking for. Also, if you’re already a Summers’ fan, you’ll like the narration and barren/harsh/hurting Summers-style protag.<br /><br />As for me: I really enjoyed the reading experience, but didn’t end up loving the book. Does this make sense?</span>

<div id="review_1407498720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407498720" />
    <a title="Eilonwy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy"><img alt="Eilonwy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506803497p2/17237503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407498720?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eilonwy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eilonwy" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy">Eilonwy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=a-bit-dark-for-me">a-bit-dark-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=character-driven">character-driven</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=diverse-characters">diverse-characters</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407498720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3032668202428800144">3-1/2 stars, rounded up. But I'm really not sure how to rate this book. <br/><br/>As everyone probably already knows, this is Courtney Summers' zombie book, and on the surface it's got the familiar elements: zombie apocalypse occurs, nearly everyone is infected almost immediately, small bands of survivors hole up and hope for the best while knowing they're probably going to meet their doom. <br/><br/>Sloane Price is one of those survivors. By sheer accident, she's fallen in with a group of five students who make it</span>
  <span id="freeText3032668202428800144" style="display:none">3-1/2 stars, rounded up. But I'm really not sure how to rate this book. <br /><br />As everyone probably already knows, this is Courtney Summers' zombie book, and on the surface it's got the familiar elements: zombie apocalypse occurs, nearly everyone is infected almost immediately, small bands of survivors hole up and hope for the best while knowing they're probably going to meet their doom. <br /><br />Sloane Price is one of those survivors. By sheer accident, she's fallen in with a group of five students who make it to the high school. <br /><br />But zombies aren't Sloane's main concern. Neither is survival. After years of physical abuse by her father, and the more recent abandonment by her older sister, Sloane is suffering trauma to the extent that she's not sure she even wants to be a survivor any longer. The troubles in her head and heart loom just as large as the troubles outside of her. <br /><br />This book felt to me like a combination of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71865.Tomorrow__When_the_War_Began__Tomorrow___1_" title="Tomorrow, When the War Began (Tomorrow, #1) by John Marsden" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tomorrow, When the War Began</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7624.Lord_of_the_Flies" title="Lord of the Flies by William Golding" rel="nofollow noopener"> Lord of the Flies</a>, as narrated by someone with severe PTSD. It's raw and harrowing, and terrible things happen. I'm not sure I "enjoyed" it. But I sure couldn't put it down, and zipped through it. I found it a different perspective and interesting twist on the typical zombie apocalypse story. Minuses are that it doesn't exactly have a plot, and it winds up very open-ended and unresolved, both zombie-wise and Sloane's internal story-wise. <br /><br />So I'm not sure how I feel about this book, at all. <br /><br />I do know that I plan to read the rest of Courtney Summers' books. She writes amazing voices, and I'd like to hear them all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3032668202428800144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_335943396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/335943396" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/335943396?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=realistic-general-or-lit-fiction">realistic-general-or-lit-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dystopia-or-apocalyptic">dystopia-or-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=hybrid-multiple-genre">hybrid-multiple-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer335943396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15052924934778645015"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I have a text message.<br/><br/>It's the end of the world and I have a text message.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Why am I not surprised? Of course the end of the world would happen and everyone would be doing whatever they could in order to hold onto the last charge on their phone, just in case that one important text message comes through.<br/><br/>3.5 stars. My advice is that you go take a spin through all of the 4 and 5 star reviews first before reading mine. I'm going to be the rare fly in the ointment who isn't completely sati</span>
  <span id="freeText15052924934778645015" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I have a text message.<br /><br />It's the end of the world and I have a text message.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Why am I not surprised? Of course the end of the world would happen and everyone would be doing whatever they could in order to hold onto the last charge on their phone, just in case that one important text message comes through.<br /><br />3.5 stars. My advice is that you go take a spin through all of the 4 and 5 star reviews first before reading mine. I'm going to be the rare fly in the ointment who isn't completely satisfied with what was trying to be accomplished here.<br /><br /><i>This is Not a Test</i> was a good book. I'll even write it again. <i>This is Not a Test</i> was a good book. It was a decent <u>realistic fiction which takes place in a post-apocalyptic world</u> book. Yes, I did go there. I'm throwing down on the genre definition. <br /><br />I was warned that the story was more about the inner workings of the characters, which didn't bother me at the time. I like reading books in which people have to battle their own inner demons. In that aspect, the story was well-crafted. But a zombie book? I really don't think that it was. And something about that fact really frustrated me. <br /><br />Anyone can take a scenario, call it end-of-the-world and then use it to throw people together in order to put them through a sort of mental hell. But when the world really doesn't extend past characters being trapped in a building, it makes me want to cry foul on the whole zombie take. Call it a natural disaster. Call it nuclear war. Call it anything but a flipping zombie book. People read zombie books because they want to see some semblance of horror or devastation. And I'm not talking about emotional devastation.<br /><br />This was not a zombie book. This was NOT a zombie book. THIS WAS NOT A ZOMBIE BOOK. And I'm still sort of pissed at that. <br /><br />However, I did like <i>This is Not a Test</i>, even though I honestly couldn't tell you why. The characters were all broken, no one really came across as likable, and the ending had us wishing we knew what was next to come. I guess this goes back to the author being able to craft a well-written story. This is how I wish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6334.Never_Let_Me_Go" title="Never Let Me Go by Kazuo Ishiguro" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Let Me Go</a> had ended - not perfectly wrapped up but at least leaving you with a tiny shred of hope.<br /><br />This one line did drive the point of the book home. Hold on to what you have while you still have time to appreciate it :<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>You can lose everything in seconds.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15052924934778645015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1195919652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195919652" />
    <a title="Kathe L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l"><img alt="Kathe L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421550107p2/25921490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1195919652?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathe L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathe L" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l">Kathe L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good">didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=fav-female-characters">fav-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1195919652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5695322476325500406">If I could give this book more than 5 stars, I would. When my brother asked me what I did today, I told him I started this amazing book at 4 p.m and finished it 10 minutes ago and that today <b>was a perfect day.</b> I feel as happy reading a book all day as I am happy staying all afternoon with a dear friend. I could tell you 11/02 was a normal day, that I went to college, talked to friends, drank coffee, studied a little, played just dance and slept. But what I will remember of today is this wonderfu</span>
  <span id="freeText5695322476325500406" style="display:none">If I could give this book more than 5 stars, I would. When my brother asked me what I did today, I told him I started this amazing book at 4 p.m and finished it 10 minutes ago and that today <b>was a perfect day.</b> I feel as happy reading a book all day as I am happy staying all afternoon with a dear friend. I could tell you 11/02 was a normal day, that I went to college, talked to friends, drank coffee, studied a little, played just dance and slept. But what I will remember of today is this wonderful book. <br><br><b>"I think she's wrong. I think this is a test. It has to be."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423701432ra/13660848.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I absolutely loved the beginning of this book. It starts as Grace and Trace (the twins), Sloane (the main girl and the one who tells the story), Cary (the "leader"), Harrison (the youngest) and Rhys (one of my favorites) are in their old school taking shelter from the zombies, because <b>this is the end of the world.</b> It is wrong to call them zombies, though. Of course, they are people who came back from the dead. But it's wrong to compare it to The Walking Dead or any other zombie book I've ever read, because this is a deeper and more thoughtful story. <b>What I always think when I read books like this (I had the same feeling with the 5th wave) is that if I would have wanted to stay alive.</b> I have this feeling that any way I explain this book it won't do it justice, but I have to try. We are introduced to Sloane, and we soon realize that she isn't ok. Who would be if everything in your life fell apart, but Sloane goes beyond that. She doesn't go right away and explains you everything that she is feeling, it is a gradual thing that keeps going on throughout the book. There's a part in the book when she and Rhys are arguing and she has a thought that goes like this: What he doesn't understand is that while he had a life that was worth it before all this, I didn't have one. <br><br><b>"But you didn't die," He says.<br><br>"I did," I say. "I'm just waiting for the rest of me to catch up.”</b><br><br>(another quote)<br><br><b>"God, when will this stop feeling so bad?"<br>"I don't thing it does. I think it's just going to be like this."</b><br><br>Sloane doesn't know why she is alive and many more people out there are not. The author explain her so well, writes her thoughts so beautifully, you can't help feeling compassion. The others have problems as well, and Trace and Cary fight every chance they have (for reasons I'm not going to tell), but which one of them deals with this situation differently. They all have big personalities and when you realize it, you are so engrossed in the story that you flinch at every harsh word, every discussion. You get teary-eyed whenever something bad happens and at every helpless thought. <br><br><b>"You just handle this. Every time I look at you, you're just taking it. And then you went outside like it was nothing. And everyone tiptoes around me. No one else made me thing about laying off Cary the way you did... no one else made me feel bad for him. It's like you see things how they need to be and you're not afraid to call it."</b><br><br>That's the best description of Sloane. But while Grace admires her (as noted in the quote above), Sloane admires Grace, Harrison admires Trace and it goes on and on. They are just trying to survive the best way they can. They are in a supposedly safe place <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was afraid at every turn of every page because of that damn window the professor broke through <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but they are not sure how long they will live. A zombie can break in at any moment. Maybe that's the last food you're eating and you don't even know it. <br><br><b>"The thing no one tells you about surviving, about the mere act of holding out, is how many hours are nothing because nothing happens. They also don't tell you about how you can share your deepest secrets with someone, kiss them, and the next hour it's like there's nothing between you because not everything can mean something all the time or you'd be crushed under the weight of it. They don't tell you how you will float through the days. You autopilot, here but not really here, sleepwalking, and then every so often you are awake."</b><br><br>I fell in love with this quote and I don't think anything else explains it better. Sloane was sad, hurt and crushed but she still yearned for things she never had, things she knew she wouldn't have in this new world but couldn't help wanting them anyway. She never let anyone deep inside her life and never told anyone all her secrets. I liked her a lot. A word to describe her? <b>She was real.</b> I dare say I never felt so much towards a character before. <br><br>I wish I could post more quotes, but I really don't want to spoil anything. I wish I convinced each one of you to read this book, and I highly suggest you guys read this review (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124624084?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>) because that's the reason I have read this one. I loved it with all my heart and I never read a book like this one. It is sad and heartbreaking but mesmerizing and captivating as well. I recommend this a lot!<br> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5695322476325500406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UYze0fqRl9l1AbeLWhuoTzibq2c0mUNgKzyB6tfVb8x0YGspcfVIkERPZy22lxtbPn4j0gsMm2ORc9SJL4HZ9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3BUDZrYhOAxgOOrbPon+4j1iV4u+EzRHdGSZpSPMV3D5+baePUXnRVF2On3SBU32O4ffPoGG7ETOK8zG25jhSg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9947943988746594835">Courtney Summers is the bestselling author of several novels, whose career in writing began in 2008, when she was 22. Her work has been released to critical acclaim and multiple starred reviews, received numerous awards and honors including the Edgar Award, the John Spray Mystery Award, the Cybils Award, the Odyssey Award, the Audie Award, and has enjoyed the recognition of many library, state, 'B</span>
  <span id="freeText9947943988746594835" style="display:none">Courtney Summers is the bestselling author of several novels, whose career in writing began in 2008, when she was 22. Her work has been released to critical acclaim and multiple starred reviews, received numerous awards and honors including the Edgar Award, the John Spray Mystery Award, the Cybils Award, the Odyssey Award, the Audie Award, and has enjoyed the recognition of many library, state, 'Best Of' and Readers' Choice lists. Courtney has reviewed for The <em>New York Times</em>, is the founder of #ToTheGirls, a 2015 worldwide trending hashtag, and in 2016, she was named one of <em>Flare</em> Magazine's 60 under 30. She lives and writes in Canada. Her new novel, <em>The Project</em> releases February 2nd, 2021 from Wednesday Books, an imprint of St. Martin's Press. You can follow her on <a href="http://instagram.com/summerscourtney" target="ig" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>, <a href="http://twitter.com/courtney_s" target="twitter" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/CourtneySummersAuthor/" target="fb" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</span>
